&lt;p&gt;Visit Adobe&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://get.adobe.com/flashplayer/&quot;&gt;Flash Player download page&lt;/a&gt; to determine which version you&amp;#8217;re using and upgrade if necessary. In recent months, Adobe has fixed a &lt;a href=&quot;https://helpx.adobe.com/security.html&quot;&gt;series of security vulnerabilities&lt;/a&gt; in Flash. At this point, it may be safer to uninstall Flash all together.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 08 Jul 2015 22:28:24 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:14;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:58:&quot;WPTavern: Stack Exchange Blog Ditches WordPress for Jekyll&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=46136&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:68:&quot;http://wptavern.com/stack-exchange-blog-ditches-wordpress-for-jekyll&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4747:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Last week Stack Exchange &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.stackexchange.com/2015/07/the-new-stack-exchange-blog/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;announced&lt;/a&gt; its new blog, revamped to publish company news and engineering posts. The first post on the blog, written by Jon Chan, Stack Overflow&amp;#8217;s developer evangelist, made no small amount of fanfare over &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.stackexchange.com/2015/07/how-we-built-our-blog/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;migrating from WordPress to Jekyll&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Chan&amp;#8217;s explanation of the team&amp;#8217;s process cites a few curious reasons for their dissatisfaction with WordPress:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;During the original proposal stage for the engineering blog, we also had a conversation about what engine we would use. At the time, all of our blogs were running WordPress&amp;#8230;which we weren&amp;#8217;t so happy about. It was very buggy, difficult to log in to, not very performant, and has caused our SRE team more than a few headaches. If we were really going to revamp the new company blog, it seemed like a lot of work to try and wrestle with our WordPress installation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;With a little bit of WordPress skill, these seem like easy complaints to resolve, especially given that Chan said the team was inspired by blogs like &lt;a href=&quot;https://codeascraft.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Code as Craft&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://oktrends.okcupid.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;OkTrends&lt;/a&gt;, both powered by WordPress. However, anti-WordPress sentiments continue to run high within the Stack Overflow community, which recently ranked the software as &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/stack-overflow-developer-survey-ranks-wordpress-as-the-3rd-most-dreaded-technology&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;the third most dreaded technology&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/get-rid-of-wp.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/get-rid-of-wp.png?resize=800%2C528&quot; alt=&quot;photo credit: StackExchange Blog&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-46331&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.stackexchange.com/2015/07/how-we-built-our-blog/&quot;&gt;StackExchange Blog&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;After a great deal of consideration, the Stack Exchange team opted to use a static engine, eventually landing on &lt;a href=&quot;http://jekyllrb.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Jekyll&lt;/a&gt;. Chan outlined the advantages they perceived in the move:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Posts are in Markdown, something most of our company was familiar with&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Jekyll is just static site generation, so it&amp;#8217;s much more performant&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Complete flexibility for front end work, no need to wrestle with templates&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Open source with a strong community, which we love&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Not WordPress or PHP&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Chan described the migration process, an endeavor that was fraught with obstacles. There is a &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/export-your-wordpress-blog-to-jekyll-with-one-click&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Jekyll Exporter plugin&lt;/a&gt; available to those who want to migrate their blogs over, but Stack Exchange opted to use the &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/thomasf/exitwp&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;exitwp&lt;/a&gt; tool to get them most of the way there.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Since Jekyll doesn&amp;#8217;t offer native support for comments, one of the biggest challenges in the migration was preserving that content and porting it into a new system. The Stack Exchange team decided to use &lt;a href=&quot;https://disqus.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Disqus&lt;/a&gt; for comments but were unable to properly migrate their existing comments and had to craft an alternative solution.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;The worst part of this is how unsupported we were by the Disqus team,&amp;#8221; Chan said. &amp;#8220;We waited on the order of weeks for support responses and for over a month they went unresolved. Sending in official support tickets, emails, and posts on their Discuss forum went unnoticed.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Despite their unsatisfactory experience with Disqus and the fact that they have to sacrifice Stack Exchange login capabilities in order to use it, Chan said they will continue with it going forward.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;re running a large, high profile blog on WordPress, it requires a certain level of expertise to customize themes and plugins and to ensure a high level of performance. It&amp;#8217;s unclear whether or not the Stack Exchange team was lacking in expertise (based on some of the complaints cited) or simply unwilling to continue with WordPress after unsatisfactory experiences. No massive migration from one platform to another is ever going to be easy and bug-free, but Chan&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.stackexchange.com/2015/07/how-we-built-our-blog/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;account&lt;/a&gt; offers some valuable insight on how difficult it currently is to move from WordPress to Jekyll while preserving all of your content.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 08 Jul 2015 21:29:45 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:15;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:47:&quot;WPTavern: HeroPress Ends Experiment With WPChat&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=46345&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:57:&quot;http://wptavern.com/heropress-ends-experiment-with-wpchat&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2781:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Since March of this year, &lt;a href=&quot;http://heropress.com/&quot;&gt;HeroPress&lt;/a&gt; has published inspirational essays from people all over the world. Instead of allowing comments on the site itself, Topher DeRosia, founder of HeroPress, partnered with &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.wpchat.com&quot;&gt;WPChat&lt;/a&gt; to host conversations for each essay. Unfortunately, many of the articles received little feedback.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Starting this week, DeRosia is allowing contributing writers &lt;a href=&quot;http://heropress.com/thoughts-on-comments/&quot;&gt;to decide&lt;/a&gt; whether they want comments enabled on their essay or not. &amp;#8220;I made the decision to have no comments because I wanted the essays to stand alone, with one voice, that being the voice of the contributor.&amp;#8221; DeRosia told the Tavern.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Directing people to a third-party site is an odd way to generate a conversation around an article. DeRosia explains why he chose to host comments on WPChat, &amp;#8220;I chose to attach WPChat to the project because it seemed like a good way for readers to express themselves without marring the surface of the essay itself.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/HeroPress3SurveyOnWPChat.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-46347&quot; src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/HeroPress3SurveyOnWPChat.png?resize=816%2C594&quot; alt=&quot;Example of a Conversation on WPChat About a HeroPress Essay&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Example of a Conversation on WPChat
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wpchat.com/t/isolated-and-intrigued-heropress-essay-3/796&quot;&gt;Isolated and intrigued&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/em&gt; as well as &lt;em&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wpchat.com/t/finding-stability-in-wordpress/893&quot;&gt;Finding stability in WordPress&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/em&gt; are two examples where great conversations took place on WPChat. However, these conversations are few and far between. &amp;#8220;That leads me to believe there could be more quality input out there and people are simply not interested in making an extra account to comment,&amp;#8221; said DeRosia.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Contributors who choose to enable comments don&amp;#8217;t need to worry about moderation. DeRosia will heavily moderate comments with a zero tolerance policy for trolls. As for WPChat hosting future conversations, DeRosia says, &amp;#8220;I like WPChat but in this case, I simply don&amp;#8217;t think it&amp;#8217;s the tool for the job.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Comments connect authors to readers and are an &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/why-comments-still-matter&quot;&gt;important part of the internet&lt;/a&gt;. Sometimes, the feedback is better than the post itself. However, requiring readers to register to a forum to comment on articles hosted on a different site is too high of a roadblock. The commenting process should be as smooth and simple as possible. Enabling comments on HeroPress is a step in the right direction.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 08 Jul 2015 20:29:18 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:16;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:23:&quot;Matt: Customer Success?&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:21:&quot;http://ma.tt/?p=45217&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:38:&quot;http://ma.tt/2015/07/customer-success/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:225:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Customer support, when done well, is a career.&amp;#8221; Automattic&amp;#8217;s support lead Andrew Spittle on &lt;a href=&quot;http://andrewspittle.com/2015/07/02/customer-success/&quot;&gt;customer success vs customer support&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 08 Jul 2015 03:00:00 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Matt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:17;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:90:&quot;WPTavern: BuiltWith Reports a 7% Increase in WordPress’ Usage from January – July 2015&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=46287&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:92:&quot;http://wptavern.com/builtwith-reports-a-7-increase-in-wordpress-usage-from-january-july-2015&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4602:&quot;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/chart.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/chart.jpg?resize=1025%2C511&quot; alt=&quot;photo credit:  Luis Llerena&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-46313&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit:  &lt;a href=&quot;https://stocksnap.io/photo/S3JE5YAMND&quot;&gt;Luis Llerena&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;BuiltWith, the popular service dedicated to monitoring internet technology trends and providing platform usage analytics, released its bi-annual &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.builtwith.com/2015/07/06/entire-internet-cms-usage-january-july-2015/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;internet coverage report for CMS usage from January &amp;#8211; July 2015&lt;/a&gt;. The report shows that WordPress, which accounts for 48% of total CMS&amp;#8217;s tracked, added 1.1 million domains since January.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;WordPress has been found on an additional 1.1 million domains since January but only accounts for a 7% increase in customer base. Whereas Ghost was added to 2,184 domain home pages and accounts for a 17% increase in their customer base.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The title of the summary is &amp;#8220;CMS Market Share Increases by Install Base,&amp;#8221; but WordPress is the only CMS shown in the chart with an actual market share value assigned based on its place among tracked competitors.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/builtwith-cms-marketshare-june-2015-report.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/builtwith-cms-marketshare-june-2015-report.png?resize=600%2C793&quot; alt=&quot;builtwith-cms-marketshare-june-2015-report&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-46289&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;BuiltWith indexed 328,852,063 domains during this quarter. Instead of simply showing the increase by usage numbers, the summary focuses on the percentage increase in customer base for a more interesting comparison. When commenters noted that this is not, in fact, market share data, Ghost co-founder John O&amp;#8217;Nolan replied, &amp;#8220;Relative growth compared to existing size is pretty much the only sane measure.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot; width=&quot;550&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/JohnONolan&quot;&gt;@JohnONolan&lt;/a&gt; Strange perspective. Ghost added 17% or 2,184 domains. WordPress added 7% or 1,149,956. That's only 535 times more sites ;)&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Aigars Silkalns (@AigarsSilkalns) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/AigarsSilkalns/status/618368722613497856&quot;&gt;July 7, 2015&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Oddly, the report did not share any figures for &lt;a href=&quot;http://trends.builtwith.com/cms/Drupal&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Drupal&lt;/a&gt; or &lt;a href=&quot;http://trends.builtwith.com/cms/Joomla!&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Joomla&lt;/a&gt;, which &lt;a href=&quot;http://w3techs.com/technologies/overview/content_management/all&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;W3techs estimates as WordPress&amp;#8217; closest CMS competitors&lt;/a&gt; in terms of market share. BuiltWith&amp;#8217;s summary appears to be limited to the fastest growing platforms based on percentage increase in customer base.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The CMS report also included some interesting stats on the WordPress versions it detected on sites indexed. These numbers roughly correspond to the project&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/about/stats/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;version usage stats&lt;/a&gt;, although WordPress doesn&amp;#8217;t publish numbers for versions older than 3.0. BuiltWith found that 1748 websites are still running on WordPress 2.1, released eight years ago. This number is down 259 sites since the beginning of the year.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/wordpress-versions.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/wordpress-versions.png?resize=600%2C545&quot; alt=&quot;photo credit: BuiltWith&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-46308&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.builtwith.com/2015/07/06/entire-internet-cms-usage-january-july-2015/&quot;&gt;BuiltWith&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;According to Gary Brewer, founder of BuiltWith, &amp;#8220;Wix and Squarespace’s main acquisition for existing websites that are using a CMS are from WordPress sites.&amp;#8221; He also notes that WordPress continues to dominate without the help of celebrity advertisements. &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mjhZ11vGl1Q&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Wix&amp;#8217;s ad with Heidi Klum&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BKIlfLReHyo&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Squarespace&amp;#8217;s Jeff Bridges commercial&lt;/a&gt;, which aired during the Super Bowl, are evidence of both companies&amp;#8217; massive marketing budgets. WordPress.com, the world&amp;#8217;s leading provider of free WordPress sites, has yet to explore that route.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 07 Jul 2015 23:05:39 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:18;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:73:&quot;WPTavern: New Proposal on Trac to Remove Post Formats from WordPress Core&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45949&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:83:&quot;http://wptavern.com/new-proposal-on-trac-to-remove-post-formats-from-wordpress-core&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4154:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Post_Formats&quot;&gt;Post Formats&lt;/a&gt; is a feature introduced in WordPress 3.1 that enables themes to visually differentiate between types of content. A&lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/post-format-history-and-wordpress-3-6&quot;&gt; metabox with radio buttons&lt;/a&gt; was added in WordPress 3.6 to expose the feature to users and allow them to easily select a format. Since WordPress 3.6 was released, there has been &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/query?status=accepted&amp;status=assigned&amp;status=closed&amp;status=new&amp;status=reopened&amp;status=reviewing&amp;component=Post+Formats&amp;order=priority&quot;&gt;little effort&lt;/a&gt; to improve the feature.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Morten Rand-Hendriksen &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-trainer-morten-rand-hendriksen-on-common-pain-points-roadblocks-and-advice-for-new-users&quot;&gt;teaches WordPress&lt;/a&gt; to thousands of people through &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.lynda.com/WordPress-tutorials/WordPress-Essential-Training/154417-2.html&quot;&gt;Lynda.com&lt;/a&gt;. After spending time writing training materials for post formats, Hendriksen was reminded of how much post formats shouldn&amp;#8217;t be in WordPress core.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He&amp;#8217;s created a &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/32844&quot;&gt;new ticket on trac&lt;/a&gt; suggesting post formats be removed from WordPress and placed into a plugin similar to how the link manager and blogroll &lt;a href=&quot;https://codex.wordpress.org/Links_Manager&quot;&gt;were removed&lt;/a&gt; in WordPress 3.5.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;After the termination of Post Formats UI, it appears the feature has largely been left to pasture and implementation across themes is at best spotty and inconsistent. One example of this is how different Post Formats are treated in the default themes, culminating in the minimalist/absent inclusion in Twenty Fifteen.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Hendriksen lists six key arguments that come up when discussing the removal of post formats from WordPress:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Feature support is inconsistent across themes causing users to wonder why the panel and options appear and disappear when themes are switched.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;When implemented, behavior is inconsistent between themes causing a perception of arbitrary or broken behavior in the eyes of the user.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Specification for what exactly each post format does is vague and ambiguous giving theme developers too much room to come up with arbitrary and non-standard behaviors that cause user confusion when themes are switched.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;The use case for Post Formats seems to have gone away or have been supplanted for the larger goal of making modular, Snowfall-like post editing available.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Post Formats behavior can be mimicked by theme developers through the use of Categories or other custom taxonomies.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Applying the &lt;a href=&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pareto_principle#In_software&quot;&gt;80/20 rule&lt;/a&gt; to software development, Hendriksen believes post formats is in the 20% range or lower. He ends the ticket by proposing post formats be moved into a feature plugin.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This would allow it to be improved concurrently with WordPress and open up opportunities to experiment with different implementations and ideas. Alternatively, it could be abandoned if no interest is shown to improve it.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Move Post Formats to a Plugin&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;My opinion of Post Formats hasn&amp;#8217;t changed since the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/why-arent-post-formats-in-wordpress-more-popular&quot;&gt;last time I wrote about them&lt;/a&gt;. They&amp;#8217;re still unpredictable, I don&amp;#8217;t see many sites using them, and they&amp;#8217;re tough to explain to new users.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Considering post formats dramatically impact the presentation of content, it&amp;#8217;s strange that the core team has not continually improved the feature after 3.6. By now, they should be rock solid. Instead, it&amp;#8217;s a feature with no obvious future.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Although you can leave a comment on this post, the best place to leave feedback is in this &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/32844&quot;&gt;trac ticket&lt;/a&gt;. It&amp;#8217;s time WordPress core developers got involved with the conversation to let us know what they think about the future of post formats in WordPress.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 07 Jul 2015 18:00:26 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:19;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:87:&quot;WPTavern: WordPress 4.3 Improves User Search and Turns Comments Off on Pages by Default&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=46238&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:97:&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-4-3-improves-user-search-and-turns-comments-off-on-pages-by-default&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4001:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-4-3-beta-1-now-available-for-testing&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordPress 4.3 beta 1&lt;/a&gt; was put into the hands of testers last week. Those who have been following 4.3 developments are already familiar with the major features headlining this release, ie. the new &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-4-3-adds-new-site-icons-feature-and-a-text-editor-to-press-this&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;site icons&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/menu-customizer-officially-approved-for-merge-into-wordpress-4-3&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;menu management in the customizer&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/32589&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;more secure passwords&lt;/a&gt;. However, there are also a couple lesser-known improvements that will have a positive impact on millions of WordPress users.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Improved User Search&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Searching for users in the admin is about to get much easier, thanks to work on a &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/27304&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;ticket&lt;/a&gt; opened by John Blackbourn 16 months ago. He notes that &amp;#8220;only the user_login (username) and user_nicename (sanitized username) fields are searched,&amp;#8221; excluding the following more likely fields:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;First name&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Last name&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Nickname&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Display name&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This issue was especially problematic in large, multi-thousand member multisite installations where finding a user in the admin often meant knowing exactly what to query and then paging through results. WordPress 4.3 contributions from &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/mordauk&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Pippin Williamson&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/wonderboymusic&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Scott Taylor&lt;/a&gt; make it possible to &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/changeset/32980&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;search by the user&amp;#8217;s email, URL, and display name&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Comments Turned Off on Pages by Default&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/comments-off-on-pages-by-default.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/comments-off-on-pages-by-default.jpg?resize=962%2C323&quot; alt=&quot;comments-off-on-pages-by-default&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-46275&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.3 will also bring a welcome change to turn off comments on pages by default. In the future when you create pages, you won&amp;#8217;t have to remember to go into the discussion settings to disable comments. One might think this would be a simple little thing to change, but quite a bit of discussion has gone into crafting the best solution to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/31168&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;ticket&lt;/a&gt; opened five months ago.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This change also applies to all custom post types. Mel Choyce outlined the new behavior in a &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2015/07/06/comments-are-now-turned-off-on-pages-by-default/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;post&lt;/a&gt; on the make.wordpress.org/core blog:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Post registrations that don’t explicitly add support for comments will now default to comments being off on new posts of that type (before, they defaulted to on). Up until now, post type support for comments has only affected admin UI; a developer could omit comment support on registration but still allow comments to be posted. &lt;strong&gt;This is a change in behavior&lt;/strong&gt;, and we will be closely monitoring its effects during beta. Moving to explicit support will allow core behavior to be more predictable and robust in the future, but we will always consider real-world usage.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The change also comes with a new function and a filter that you can use to restore the current behavior of comments to your post type, if necessary. More details and an example on how to use the filter are available on the make.wordpress.org/core announcement &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2015/07/06/comments-are-now-turned-off-on-pages-by-default/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;post&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 07 Jul 2015 05:07:42 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:20;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:20:&quot;Matt:
