&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 02 Jul 2015 16:35:04 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:36;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:75:&quot;WPTavern: Ship: A New App for Shipping Plugins from GitHub to WordPress.org&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=46018&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:84:&quot;http://wptavern.com/ship-a-new-app-for-shipping-plugins-from-github-to-wordpress-org&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4863:&quot;&lt;p&gt;One of the small hurdles to hosting a plugin on WordPress.org is the fact that you have to use SVN to ship your updates. Most developers are far more familiar with Git. It&amp;#8217;s not difficult to learn how to use SVN for the sake of WordPress.org plugins, but many find it to be inconvenient.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://ship.getherbert.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Ship&lt;/a&gt; is a new application designed to eliminate this hassle by helping developers ship plugins directly from GitHub to WordPress.org. All you have to do is tag the release on GitHub and the app will automatically push updates to the plugin&amp;#8217;s official SVN repo on WordPress.org.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/ship.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/ship.png?resize=1025%2C641&quot; alt=&quot;ship&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-46026&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The application was created by &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/jasonagnew__&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Jason Agnew&lt;/a&gt; and his team at &lt;a href=&quot;http://bigbitecreative.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Big Bite Creative&lt;/a&gt;, authors of the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/herbert-a-new-wordpress-plugin-framework&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Herbert plugin framework&lt;/a&gt;. The team built the app in Laravel in just five days. It&amp;#8217;s currently hosted on Digital Ocean, but Agnew plans to move it over to AWS once Ship has gained more users.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;We’ve reached a point where most developers are familiar with GitHub, and as a result, Git,&amp;#8221; Agnew said in his &lt;a href=&quot;http://bigbitecreative.com/introducing-ship-publishing-your-wordpress-plugin/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;announcement&lt;/a&gt;. &amp;#8220;If you plan to do anything open source you’re likely to find yourself on there &amp;#8211; even Apple has made the move. Unfortunately WordPress.org uses SVN, which most developers don’t use daily, or are even familiar with. It’s easy enough to pick up, but why should you learn something new to update your plugin?&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;With the help of the Ship app, developers won&amp;#8217;t have to touch SVN at all during the process of sending updates to WordPress.org plugin repositories.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;For years most plugin developers have used GitHub and then shipped to WordPress.org SVN using a bash script,&amp;#8221; Agnew said. &amp;#8220;You’ll find plenty out there, but they require you to keep both a Git and SVN repo on your machine — plus you need to remember to run it every time you tag a new release. We thought there must be a simpler way to do this, so we put our heads together. After a few days we had put together the first version of Ship.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In order to use the app you must have already &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/add/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;submitted your plugin zip file to WordPress.org&lt;/a&gt;. You can then sign into the &lt;a href=&quot;http://ship.getherbert.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Ship&lt;/a&gt; app with GitHub and authorize its access to your repositories.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/authorize-ship-app.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/authorize-ship-app.jpg?resize=716%2C434&quot; alt=&quot;authorize-ship-app&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-46044&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The app will then fetch your repositories and you&amp;#8217;ll have the opportunity to select the ones you want to link up with a WordPress.org SVN address in order to start syncing updates.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/ship-sync-reops.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/ship-sync-reops.jpg?resize=842%2C525&quot; alt=&quot;ship-sync-reops&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-46046&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Big Bite Creative has built many custom plugins over the years, but Agnew said they never had the time to open source them.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Now with Herbert out there we want to start releasing more plugins on Github &amp;#8211; Ship is part of making that process easier,&amp;#8221; he said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In the future, Agnew and his team would like to eliminate the need to first submit your plugin on WordPress.org and instead have that process initiated by Ship. They used &amp;#8220;Sign in with GitHub&amp;#8221; to save time when initially building the app but would also like to open it up for other services like BitBucket.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The new Ship app effectively gets around WordPress.org&amp;#8217;s SVN requirement for plugin repos, which has long been a minor deterrent and annoyance for developers wanting to host their work in the directory. If Ship is successful in making plugin developer&amp;#8217;s lives easier, the result will be more open source extensions available to WordPress users. Agnew and his team welcome feedback on the app and have created &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/getherbert/ship&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;an empty repo on GiHub&lt;/a&gt; to capture any suggestions or issues.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 02 Jul 2015 01:13:14 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:37;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:64:&quot;WPTavern: Which One of These Six Cities Should Host WordCamp US?&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=46027&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:73:&quot;http://wptavern.com/which-one-of-these-six-cities-should-host-wordcamp-us&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1498:&quot;&lt;p&gt;When Matt Mullenweg &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordcamp-us-2015-now-accepting-applications-for-host-city&quot;&gt;put out the call&lt;/a&gt; to cities interested in hosting WordCamp US, we learned the criteria they would have to meet in order to qualify. Venues would need to seat approximately 1,000-2,00 people, have hotels within 3 miles of the venue, hotel costs for a range of budgets, and average flight costs from the West Coast, East Coast, Midwest, Mexico, and Canada.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Applications to host WordCamp US 2015 &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/community/2015/07/01/wordcamp-us-update/&quot;&gt;officially closed today&lt;/a&gt;. Six cities submitted applications to host the event, they include:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Chattanooga&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Chicago&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Detroit&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Orlando&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Philadelphia&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Phoenix&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;On the Make WordPress Community site, Cami Kaos says applications are being carefully reviewed and organizers of the host city will be contacted as soon as possible. Dates for the event won&amp;#8217;t be given until a host city and venue is chosen.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Out of all the cities selected, I want WordCamp US to be in Chicago. I love Chicago and it&amp;#8217;s a quick flight from Cleveland. The city also has awesome pizza. Take the poll below and vote for which city you think should host WordCamp US. This poll is only for fun and will not affect the outcome of the host city.&lt;/p&gt;
Note: There is a poll embedded within this post, please visit the site to participate in this post's poll.&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 02 Jul 2015 00:28:51 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:38;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:65:&quot;WPTavern: It’s Not a WordPress Problem, It’s a People Problem&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=46019&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:68:&quot;http://wptavern.com/its-not-a-wordpress-problem-its-a-people-problem&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1503:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Tom McFarlin &lt;a href=&quot;https://tommcfarlin.com/the-wordpress-community-a-comedy-of-drama-ego-oligarchies-and-more/&quot;&gt;published a thoughtful piece&lt;/a&gt; on what he perceives to be the sad state of the WordPress community. Too many people are participating in behavior that is embarrassing from the outside looking in. It&amp;#8217;s a long read, but it highlights the need for members of the WordPress community to stop and reflect on our actions.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The WordPress community is described by many as being open, friendly, with a willingness to help. It&amp;#8217;s all of those things but in the past few months, discussions on hotly debated topics such as the Customizer have brought the worst out of people.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Criticism is one thing, personal attacks are another and simply unnecessary. Unfortunately, text is a difficult medium to decipher context. Emoticons and emoji help, but it doesn&amp;#8217;t solve the problem. We as a community need to approach discussions with open minds. We can have different perspectives and viewpoints but we need to clearly communicate them without tearing the opposition down in the process. We must also learn to agree to disagree.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;McFarlin&amp;#8217;s post is an inward facing moment for the WordPress community. Is this how we want people on the outside to portray us? WordPress is software created by passionate people who work tirelessly to improve the web. Let&amp;#8217;s all take a deep breath, collect ourselves, and do more to listen and understand each other.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 01 Jul 2015 23:21:27 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:39;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:83:&quot;WPTavern: WordPress 4.3 Adds New Site Icons Feature and a Text Editor to Press This&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45992&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:93:&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-4-3-adds-new-site-icons-feature-and-a-text-editor-to-press-this&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3433:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.3 is on track to include a new site icons feature, which will allow administrators to easily upload an image to be used as the favicon and app icons for a site. Favicons have traditionally been handled by WordPress themes or plugins, but the new core support means that users no longer have to hunt down an extension to handle this basic site feature.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This addition landed in 4.3 in response to a four-year old trac &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/16434&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;ticket&lt;/a&gt; requesting an easier way for non-technical users to upload and crop an image to use as a favicon. Konstantin Obenland, release lead for 4.3, &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/changeset/32994&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;committed the feature to WordPress trunk&lt;/a&gt; this week, along with the following summary of its current capabilities:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;This v1 marries Jetpack&amp;#8217;s Site Icon module with the Media Modal, reusing code from the Custom Header admin. For now, the core-provided icons will be limited to a favicon, an iOS app icon, and a Windows tile icon, leaving .ico support and additional icons to plugins to add.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;After testing WordPress 4.3-alpha, I found that the experience of adding a favicon in the settings panel is smoother and more intuitive than any plugin I&amp;#8217;ve ever tried. The screen offers users a nice preview of the image as a favicon and mobile icon. It also doesn&amp;#8217;t burden you with any notices about sizes and image quality, unless you attempt to upload an image that is less than 512px in width.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/wordpress-site-icon.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/wordpress-site-icon.jpg?resize=848%2C691&quot; alt=&quot;wordpress-site-icon&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-46000&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you want to test the feature, you can provide feedback on the &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/16434&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;ticket&lt;/a&gt; or via the announcement &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2015/06/30/today-in-the-nightly-site-icons-text-editor-in-press-this/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;post&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Another major enhancement added to 4.3 this week is a text editor for Press This. Many WordPress users appreciate the streamlined simplicity of the Press This post editor but were held back from using it to compose posts due to the lack of HTML editing support. The addition of a text editor offers the same capabilities as the standard editor in &lt;em&gt;post-new.php&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/press-this-text-editor.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/press-this-text-editor.jpg?resize=1025%2C466&quot; alt=&quot;press-this-text-editor&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-46007&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Press This will also receive a few &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/changeset/32999&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;polishes&lt;/a&gt; in addition to the text editor, including auto-scrolling when the caret moves out of the viewport while the user is typing (similar to editor-expand) and auto-resizing for the textarea. WordPress 4.3&amp;#8217;s improvements to Press This are not exactly a replacement for the dearly-departed distraction-free writing mode, but the post editor at &lt;em&gt;wp-admin/press-this.php&lt;/em&gt; is quickly becoming one of the more zen-like interfaces in the admin.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 01 Jul 2015 20:50:03 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:40;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:24:&quot;Matt: Safari the new IE?&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:21:&quot;http://ma.tt/?p=45200&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:39:&quot;http://ma.tt/2015/07/safari-the-new-ie/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:291:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;In recent years, Apple’s strategy towards the web can most charitably be described as &amp;#8216;benevolent neglect.'&amp;#8221; &lt;a href=&quot;http://nolanlawson.com/2015/06/30/safari-is-the-new-ie/&quot;&gt;Nolan Lawson throws the gauntlet down by asking Is Safari the new Internet Explorer?&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 01 Jul 2015 18:28:29 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Matt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:41;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:27:&quot;Matt: Mood&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:21:&quot;http://ma.tt/?p=45193&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:43:&quot;http://ma.tt/2015/06/gut-bacteria-and-mood/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:179:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nytimes.com/2015/06/28/magazine/can-the-bacteria-in-your-gut-explain-your-mood.html&quot;&gt;Can the Bacteria in Your Gut Explain Your Mood?&lt;/a&gt; Answer: Maybe.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Matt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:42;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:98:&quot;WPTavern: WordPress for iOS 5.3 Released With Refreshed Stats and a New Layout for Posts and Pages&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45958&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:108:&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-for-ios-5-3-released-with-refreshed-stats-and-a-new-layout-for-posts-and-pages&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2620:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress for iOS 5.3 &lt;a href=&quot;https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/wordpress/id335703880?mt=8&amp;uo=6&amp;at=&amp;ct=&quot;&gt;is available on iTunes&lt;/a&gt; and has a few new features. Post listings display more content making them easier to browse. A search feature has been added to the post listing screen that displays results as you type.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/WordPressForIos53Search.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-45969&quot; src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/WordPressForIos53Search.png?resize=281%2C500&quot; alt=&quot;Search bar in WordPress for iOS 5.3&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Search bar in WordPress for iOS 5.3
&lt;p&gt;I tested the search feature on two different sites. The first site is on WordPress.com and doesn&amp;#8217;t use featured images. Search results displayed quickly with little lag.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The second is a self hosted WordPress site that uses featured images. I noticed lag as the app tried to display real-time results as I typed which also lagged the app. I couldn&amp;#8217;t do anything else within the app until the search query finished.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I don&amp;#8217;t use the search feature often and this experience has me concerned. Instead of being fast and fluid, it&amp;#8217;s chunky and slow. I also don&amp;#8217;t see the need to display featured images in search results. I think this would make the search query and the app faster.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress.com and self hosted WordPress sites are now combined under My Sites. Instead of seeing a spinning circle when checking stats, there&amp;#8217;s a progress bar at the top. This gives the appearance that the stats page loads faster. The stats page also has a subtle color scheme change that makes things more pronounced.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/WordPressiOS53StatsPage.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-45975&quot; src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/WordPressiOS53StatsPage.png?resize=281%2C500&quot; alt=&quot;WordPress for iOS 5.3 Stats Page&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;WordPress for iOS 5.3 Stats Page
&lt;p&gt;Last but not least, 5.3 includes &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/wordpress-mobile/WordPress-iOS/issues?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;q=is%3Aclosed+is%3Aissue+milestone%3A5.3+label%3Abug+&quot;&gt;several bug fixes&lt;/a&gt;. Overall, 5.3 is a decent update. Remember to use caution when searching a site with a lot of posts that use featured images. WordPress for iOS 5.3 &lt;a href=&quot;https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/wordpress/id335703880?mt=8&amp;uo=6&amp;at=&amp;ct=&quot;&gt;is available for free on iTunes&lt;/a&gt;. If you encounter any issues in 5.3, please report them &lt;a href=&quot;https://ios.forums.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;in the support forum&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 01 Jul 2015 00:26:29 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:43;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:70:&quot;WPTavern: Filter to Disable the Customizer Shot Down on WordPress Trac&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45837&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:80:&quot;http://wptavern.com/filter-to-disable-the-customizer-shot-down-on-wordpress-trac&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:7716:&quot;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/do-not-shut-off.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/do-not-shut-off.jpg?resize=823%2C420&quot; alt=&quot;photo credit: shutoff - (license)&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-45971&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.flickr.com/photos/86846941@N00/404597014&quot;&gt;shutoff&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; &lt;a href=&quot;https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/2.0/&quot;&gt;(license)&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.3 will &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/menu-customizer-officially-approved-for-merge-into-wordpress-4-3&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;introduce menu management via the customizer&lt;/a&gt;, providing live previews on the frontend for adding, deleting, and ordering menu items. Although users still have the option to manage menus using the admin interface, developers who are not keen on the feature are searching for an easy way to disable the customizer and remove its links throughout WordPress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In certain scenarios involving client work, the customizer can be more trouble than it&amp;#8217;s worth and may not be a beneficial addition to a custom-tailored WordPress admin.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot; width=&quot;550&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/pollyplummer&quot;&gt;@pollyplummer&lt;/a&gt; very interesting. I'm not against the new updates but the customizer is hell in the agency world.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Edward McIntyre (@twittem) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/twittem/status/613500444162195456&quot;&gt;June 24, 2015&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hereswhatidid&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Gabe Shackle&lt;/a&gt;, an application developer and UI engineer at &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.risdall.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Risdall&lt;/a&gt;, created a &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/32772&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;ticket&lt;/a&gt; on WordPress trac last week, requesting a filter to disable the customizer. His patch offers developers an easy way to enable the &amp;#8216;no-customizer-support&amp;#8217; class within the body tag.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Due to the fact that the &amp;#8216;customizer-support&amp;#8217; class is added via JavaScript on page render, it cannot be manipulated using any core filters or actions currently.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;By setting the filter value to false, the Customizer is essentially hidden from the admin and the links that were currently pointing at the Customizer (widgets, themes, etc&amp;#8230;) are reverted to their previous dashboard destinations.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Currently, developers who want to disable the customizer have to employ a combination of different methods in order to effectively remove everything that the customizer introduces into the admin.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;This filter makes this process into a simple boolean filter so that developers who do not want or need the Customizer can easily remove it,&amp;#8221; Shackle said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress lead developer &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/dd32&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Dion Hulse&lt;/a&gt; replied to the ticket to say that although he doesn&amp;#8217;t use the customizer much himself, he doesn&amp;#8217;t think that WordPress users would benefit from an easy way to turn it off.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Personally as much as I don&amp;#8217;t use the customizer a lot of the time, I think offering a filter to disable it is probably not in the best interests of WordPress users.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The customizer, as much as some dislike it, is a major component of the future of WordPress UX &amp;#8211; whether that is a good or bad thing remains to be seen by some &amp;#8211; but like it or hate it, it&amp;#8217;s here.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Hulse &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/32772#comment:1&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;suggested&lt;/a&gt;, as an alternative, that a better way to disable it would be to remove the &lt;code&gt;customize&lt;/code&gt; capability from the roles.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Shackle further explained that he was attempting to follow the precedent of the admin bar, which he considers to be a similar type of UX component.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;The Admin Bar can be disabled not only by a filter but by a global variable, core function, and user profile setting,&amp;#8221; he said. &amp;#8220;The Customizer has none of these options.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Nick Halsey, the developer of the Menu Customizer plugin that is being merged into 4.3, &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/32772#comment:3&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;replied&lt;/a&gt; based on assumptions about why Shackle might request a filter to disable the feature:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;I have yet to see a valid reason for something like this. In most cases, concerns about not wanting users to have access to the Customizer stem from the fact that you&amp;#8217;re not giving them the appropriate capabilities. And the customize capability can be used to turn off the Customizer if you really must.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;While you can remove the customize meta capability (or re-map it or whatever), doing so simply because you don&amp;#8217;t want to train users or don&amp;#8217;t want to use the Customizer is doing yourself and your users an enormous disservice. As dd32 mentioned, the Customizer will only continue to grow in importance within WordPress. Additionally, user testing has shown that the Customizer experience is generally easier for users to grasp than the admin, which largely stems from the value of having live-previewing available. We&amp;#8217;re putting a significant amount of time into the Customizer every release to continue improving it, conducting frequent user tests along the way to optimize usability.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Halsey promptly closed the ticket following this exchange. I followed up with Shackle to find out why the proposed alternative to remove the &lt;code&gt;customize&lt;/code&gt; capability is inadequate for his purposes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Mostly I was hoping that the Customizer could be treated more like the admin bar, which has 3+ methods for disabling it,&amp;#8221; Shackle said. &amp;#8220;Having a clearly labeled filter is, in my opinion, more legible than modifying user capabilities. A PHP developer with virtually no WordPress knowledge could most likely understand much quicker what&amp;#8217;s happening with a filter named &amp;#8216;enable_customizer_support&amp;#8217; rather than &amp;#8216;map_meta_cap&amp;#8217;.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Obviously, not all tickets and patches will be considered valid by the maintainers of WordPress core components, but Shackle was disappointed by the defensive response to the discussion.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Honestly, had the reply simply been something along the lines of &amp;#8216;You should just use the &lt;code&gt;customize&lt;/code&gt; capability to achieve the same effect&amp;#8217; I really wouldn&amp;#8217;t have had any issue,&amp;#8221; he said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Unfortunately, it seems any approach other than &amp;#8216;Customizer for all things!&amp;#8217; means I get to be told multiple times how much of a disservice I&amp;#8217;m doing my clients and what a lazy developer I am for not just re-training my clients how to manage their sites&amp;#8217; appearance.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;It feels like the Customizer team themselves have an all-or-nothing approach to the project and that anyone who questions this is wrong, regardless of their reasoning,&amp;#8221; Shackle said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This exchange demonstrates that since core contributors view the customizer as a major part of the future of WordPress, this is one feature where there will be little willingness to support efforts to make it more modular. Disabling support for the customizer will continue to require use of &amp;#8216;map_meta_cap,&amp;#8217; the same &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/parallelus/customizer-remove-all-parts/blob/master/wp-crap.php#L75&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;method&lt;/a&gt; the creators of the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/new-plugin-removes-all-traces-of-the-customizer-in-wordpress&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Customizer Remove All Parts&lt;/a&gt; plugin have employed.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 30 Jun 2015 23:08:12 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:44;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:72:&quot;WPTavern: UpThemes Adds Managed WordPress Hosting to Theme Club Business&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45775&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:82:&quot;http://wptavern.com/upthemes-adds-managed-wordpress-hosting-to-theme-club-business&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4711:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/upthemes.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/upthemes.jpg?resize=665%2C300&quot; alt=&quot;upthemes&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-45946&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;After five years of selling themes and support, UpThemes is branching out into the managed WordPress hosting business. Last week the company &lt;a href=&quot;https://upthemes.com/blog/2015/06/upthemes-hosting/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;announced&lt;/a&gt; the new hosting venture and partnership with &lt;a href=&quot;http://aesopstoryengine.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Aesop Interactive&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;We are excited to announce UpThemes Hosting, a managed WordPress hosting solution that includes 40+ premium WordPress themes including our entire theme library, all themes from the collection of Aesop Interactive (makers of Aesop Story Engine), as well as a curated selection of beautifully-designed themes from WordPress.org.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;For &lt;a href=&quot;https://upthemes.com/hosting/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;$20/month&lt;/a&gt; customers can host one WordPress site with 5GB disk space and 100GB monthly bandwith. Tech support is included along with 40+ commercial themes from UpThemes and Aesop Interactive. Users have control over their sites as they would with a standard WordPress installation, i.e. FTP access, ability to install plugins and themes, etc.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/upthemes-hosting.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/upthemes-hosting.png?resize=640%2C647&quot; alt=&quot;upthemes-hosting&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-45944&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;This is actually a partnership with &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.pressed.net/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Pressed.net&lt;/a&gt;, a division of &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.site5.com/p/wordpress/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Site5&lt;/a&gt;, that sits on top of their managed WordPress hosting architecture,&amp;#8221; UpThemes co-founder Chris Wallace told the Tavern. &amp;#8220;We&amp;#8217;ve looked at many opportunities for a hosting partnership over the years and none of the options felt quite right to us, so we waited until there was one that provided our customers with the best hosting service and support.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Site5 understood that need and we&amp;#8217;ve worked hand-in-hand for many months to finally release this product. We&amp;#8217;re very proud of it and think it provides more value than the typical WordPress hosting product.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The hybrid combination of hosting plus a theme club is fairly unique in the WordPress ecosystem, but Wallace believes it provides an easier path for UpThemes customers looking to build an online presence.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Our audience is mainly DIYers who just need a site up and running,&amp;#8221; he said. &amp;#8220;We&amp;#8217;ve always been looking to make it as easy as possible to purchase and install an UpThemes theme so a hosting platform where all our themes are pre-installed seemed like the perfect solution to the problem of &amp;#8216;which theme do I pick&amp;#8217; and &amp;#8216;how do I install a theme&amp;#8217; and &amp;#8216;will your theme work on my webhost?'&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The new hosting product also helps UpThemes deal with the financial volatility and unpredictability of managing a theme club business.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;From a business perspective, selling themes alone has always made it difficult to pin down our customer acquisition cost and churn rate (meaning the number of customers who stop paying their annual renewals),&amp;#8221; Wallace said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Since we offer an annual license, we don&amp;#8217;t know if a customer will renew for a whole year, which, as you can imagine, makes it hard to know the lifetime value of the customer. It&amp;#8217;s a hard thing to analyze. Some people care enough to renew but most people don&amp;#8217;t understand the value enough to care.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;UpThemes will continue to serve the small business and DIY market and Wallace hopes to add more journalists, storytellers, and photographers with the new Aesop Interactive partnership.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Beyond our new hosting venture, we also serve thousands of blogs on WordPress.com, which helps us offer a one-click method of buying and using our themes without any sort of installation required,&amp;#8221; Wallace said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;I think that really is one of the key points for us: closing the gap on how much knowledge you need to use our themes. We&amp;#8217;d like to make it even easier for certain types of customers (e-commerce, for example) to hit the ground running.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;There are so many variables to creating a successful online business and we just want to give less technical WordPress users an easier path to success.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 30 Jun 2015 17:54:24 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:45;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:30:&quot;Matt: Loyalists vs Mercenaries&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:21:&quot;http://ma.tt/?p=45198&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:46:&quot;http://ma.tt/2015/06/loyalists-vs-mercenaries/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:853:&quot;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Finally, think about being somewhere other than the Bay Area or NYC. Yes, they are great places to start companies, find talent, and get investment. But they are also places where others start companies, get investment, and find your talent. It’s a ratrace, a treadmill, and it’s grueling. If you can avoid it, you owe it to yourself to try.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Fred Wilson on &lt;a href=&quot;http://avc.com/2015/06/loyalists-vs-mercenaries/&quot;&gt;Loyalists vs Mercenaries in companies&lt;/a&gt;. I&amp;#8217;m so happy to see the non-SF/NYC company idea continue to pick up steam, and I think its natural conclusion is distributed work as Automattic does. Like any relationship, I think the most rewarding employee/employer relationships are the ones that grow &lt;a href=&quot;http://ma.tt/2015/06/ten-years-of-automattic/&quot;&gt;over decades&lt;/a&gt;, not just years.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 30 Jun 2015 06:00:00 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Matt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:46;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:80:&quot;WPTavern: The Recommended Hosting Page on WordPress.org Starts Over From Scratch&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45904&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:90:&quot;http://wptavern.com/the-recommended-hosting-page-on-wordpress-org-starts-over-from-scratch&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4803:&quot;&lt;p&gt;One of the most difficult tasks for new WordPress users is choosing a good webhost. The process can involve getting recommendations from friends, searching Google for reviews, and taking advantage of trial offers. Since 2005, WordPress.org has had a &lt;a href=&quot;https://web.archive.org/web/20050913180027/http://wordpress.org/hosting/&quot;&gt;recommended hosts page&lt;/a&gt; featuring companies that meet certain criteria.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/WordPressRecommendedHosts2005.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-45906&quot; src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/WordPressRecommendedHosts2005.png?resize=761%2C841&quot; alt=&quot;WordPress.org Recommended Host Page in 2005&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;WordPress.org Recommended Host Page in 2005
&lt;p&gt;Over the years, new companies would rarely be added to the page. For several years, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.bluehost.com/&quot;&gt;Bluehost&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.dreamhost.com/home.2.html&quot;&gt;DreamHost&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=&quot;http://laughingsquid.com/&quot;&gt;Laughing Squid&lt;/a&gt; were the only companies listed.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/RecommendedHostsIn2014.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-45907&quot; src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/RecommendedHostsIn2014.png?resize=727%2C600&quot; alt=&quot;Recommend Hosts Page in 2014&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Recommend Hosts Page in 2014
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;ve spoken to a number of people in the webhosting industry in the last two years and the general consensus is that, to get on the list, you need to pay Matt Mullenweg a lot of money, which isn&amp;#8217;t true. Bluehost is often used as an example as they&amp;#8217;re owned by &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.endurance.com/&quot;&gt;Endurance International Group&lt;/a&gt; who &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.prweb.com/releases/2014/05/prweb11874425.htm&quot;&gt;invested in Automattic&lt;/a&gt; in 2014. Bluehost has been on the list since 2005, long before any investment took place.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;A Fresh Start to The Recommended Hosts Page&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Currently, Bluehost is the only recommended webhost &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/hosting/&quot;&gt;on the&lt;/a&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/hosting/&quot;&gt; page&lt;/a&gt; because it&amp;#8217;s going through a revamp. Near the bottom of the page is a paragraph that admits a lot has changed in the industry over the years.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Much has changed in the hosting world since this page was originally set up. There are now many types of dedicated and cloud accounts that are as easy as shared hosting was a generation ago, and shared and managed hosts have evolved significantly to become more tailored to WordPress. WordPress is often now the most commonly used application on major web hosts!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I asked Mullenweg if hosts that were on the page before are eligible to be re-added, &amp;#8220;Of course, anyone is up for consideration and Bluehost is up for being removed.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The WordPress.org team is starting over from scratch and as such, webhosting companies are asked to complete &lt;a href=&quot;http://mcm.polldaddy.com/s/2015-wordpress-hosting-survey&quot;&gt;the following&lt;/a&gt; survey by &lt;strong&gt;July 31st&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/FirstPageofTheSurvey.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-45908&quot; src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/FirstPageofTheSurvey.png?resize=616%2C415&quot; alt=&quot;First Page of The Survey&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;First Page of The Survey
&lt;p&gt;The survey is 40 questions long and includes questions such as:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;What&amp;#8217;s the WordPress-specific landing page you&amp;#8217;d want /hosting to point to?&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;What type of customers do you target?&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Please describe your technology stack, and why you like it.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Is 100% of the code included or promoted with your WordPress install GPL or compatible?&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It may seem like a tedious process, but those I&amp;#8217;ve spoken to in the past affiliated with companies once on the list say it generates thousands to millions of dollars in signups. This should motivate companies to complete the survey accurately. Even if a company is not listed on the page, those who fill out the survey will be giving WordPress.org a lot of information that may come in handy for other uses.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;It&amp;#8217;s About Time&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The recommended hosting page is long overdue for a revamp. There are companies such as, A2 Hosting, Pagely, WP Engine, InMotion Hosting, and countless others that are doing a great job hosting large and small WordPress sites. Perhaps it&amp;#8217;s time they become the ones recommended instead of the standard three. If you own or operate a webhosting company with an emphasis on WordPress, &lt;a href=&quot;http://mcm.polldaddy.com/s/2015-wordpress-hosting-survey&quot;&gt;fill out the survey&lt;/a&gt;, as it&amp;#8217;s the best chance you have to getting on the recommended hosts page.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 30 Jun 2015 03:52:35 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:47;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:80:&quot;WPTavern: VaultPress Comes Out on Top in Recent Survey of WordPress Backup Tools&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45874&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:90:&quot;http://wptavern.com/vaultpress-comes-out-on-top-in-recent-survey-of-wordpress-backup-tools&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2207:&quot;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/VaultFeaturesImage.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-45875&quot; src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/VaultFeaturesImage.png?resize=647%2C363&quot; alt=&quot;Vault Featured Image&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.flickr.com/photos/37053322@N00/2291139919&quot;&gt;Code&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; &lt;a href=&quot;https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/2.0/&quot;&gt;(license)&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Steven Gliebe asked 21 WordPress professionals what they use to generate backups for their personal sites and published the results on the &lt;a href=&quot;https://proplugindirectory.com/best-backup-wordpress-plugins/&quot;&gt;Pro Plugin Directory blog&lt;/a&gt;. The results are split into two groups of people &amp;#8211; writers and developers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;All of the writers mentioned &lt;a href=&quot;https://vaultpress.com/&quot;&gt;VaultPress&lt;/a&gt; as their go-to backup solution. Some of the developers use VaultPress but most rely on backups generated by their webhost in addition to a plugin or custom strategy. &lt;a href=&quot;https://ithemes.com/purchase/backupbuddy/&quot;&gt;BackupBuddy &lt;/a&gt;by iThemes ended up with the second most mentions.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Although &lt;a href=&quot;https://deliciousbrains.com/wp-migrate-db-pro/&quot;&gt;WP Migrate DB Pro&lt;/a&gt; is used primarily to migrate WordPress sites, Gilbert Pellegrom of &lt;a href=&quot;http://dev7studios.com/&quot;&gt;Dev7studios,&lt;/a&gt; uses it to backup his databases and user uploads with a setup &lt;a href=&quot;https://deliciousbrains.com/remotely-backup-wordpress-database-media-wp-migrate-db-pro-cli/&quot;&gt;similar to this&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Bill Robbins of &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.organizedthemes.com/&quot;&gt;Organized Themes,&lt;/a&gt; says WPEngine provides a prompt reminding users to generate a full backup before upgrading. This sounds like a great idea and is something I think more hosts should look into doing. Daniel Espinoza of &lt;a href=&quot;https://shopplugins.com/&quot;&gt;Shop Plugins,&lt;/a&gt; uses a backup strategy that allows him to &lt;strong&gt;own his data&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To learn &lt;strong&gt;why&lt;/strong&gt; these 21 people use the backup strategies that they do, I encourage you to &lt;a href=&quot;https://proplugindirectory.com/best-backup-wordpress-plugins/&quot;&gt;read the full article&lt;/a&gt;. What plugins and services do you use to backup your sites?&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 29 Jun 2015 22:40:26 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:48;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:72:&quot;WPTavern: Theme Hybrid Experiments with Free Signups for Club Membership&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45871&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:82:&quot;http://wptavern.com/theme-hybrid-experiments-with-free-signups-for-club-membership&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3870:&quot;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/open-source.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/open-source.jpg?resize=1024%2C514&quot; alt=&quot;photo credit: 16th st - (license)&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-45884&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.flickr.com/photos/79777096@N00/6866996865&quot;&gt;16th st&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; &lt;a href=&quot;https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nd/2.0/&quot;&gt;(license)&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Justin Tadlock, creator of Theme Hybrid, &lt;a href=&quot;http://themehybrid.com/weblog/steering-the-ship-back-home&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;announced&lt;/a&gt; today that the seven year old theme club is experimenting with a radical change in club pricing. &lt;a href=&quot;http://themehybrid.com/club&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Club membership&lt;/a&gt; is now free for anyone who wants to sign up. Although Theme Hybrid&amp;#8217;s plugins and themes have always been free, standard club membership (which includes access to the support forums), was previously $25/year.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In a post titled &amp;#8220;&lt;a href=&quot;http://themehybrid.com/weblog/steering-the-ship-back-home&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Steering the Ship Back Home&lt;/a&gt;,&amp;#8221; Tadlock explains his original purpose for the club. Theme Hybrid entered the WordPress theme market with free, open source products back in the day when very few commercial theme sellers were fully adopting the GPL.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;When I first laid the groundwork for Theme Hybrid, or &lt;a href=&quot;http://justintadlock.com/archives/2008/05/31/project-m&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Project M&lt;/a&gt; as it was originally called, seven awesome years ago, the idea was to face off against &amp;#8216;premium&amp;#8217; theme authors,&amp;#8221; he said. &amp;#8220;I wanted to provide a free alternative to the marketplace and show that it could work.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Tadlock described how, overall, the Theme Hybrid experience has been positive, but during the past year he faced creative blocks, burnout, and a lack of focus. As part of regaining motivation, he decided to refocus Theme Hybrid back to its radical roots.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;I always knew I wanted to provide awesome free/$free WordPress themes and plugins,&amp;#8221; he said. &amp;#8220;However, $free doesn’t exactly put food on the table. While seven years has been a good run, I don’t think I ever found the right balance between philosophy and practical concerns.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As part of a fresh start, Tadlock is opening up his club membership in an effort to expand the community that has kept the site going over the years. In addition to the free memberships, which provide access to the forums, he is also slashing prices on the tiered memberships.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Today, I have at least a couple of months of wiggle room to try something new while figuring out the direction I want to take the business aspect of this site,&amp;#8221; Tadlock said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Theme Hybrid&amp;#8217;s radical shift in club pricing is another example of WordPress businesses giving away more for free, whether it be &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/lasso-frontend-editing-plugin-for-wordpress-now-available-on-github&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;commercial products on GitHub&lt;/a&gt;, a &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/all-official-easy-digital-downloads-themes-are-now-100-free&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;suite of e-commerce themes&lt;/a&gt;, or &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wpsessions-changes-pricing-structure-live-events-are-now-100-free&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;live training events&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Theme Hybrid has always erred on the side of providing free products and tutorials for the community, as opposed to locking them up. Will giving away more for free translate into a higher number of people willing to pay for support? This question is at the core of the freemium business model, the boundaries of which Tadlock has been willing to push for the past seven years.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;While trying new things is certainly frightening, I’m excited about some of the prospects,&amp;#8221; he said.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 29 Jun 2015 21:45:49 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:49;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:54:&quot;WPTavern: Vienna, Austria to Host WordCamp Europe 2016&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=45834&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:63:&quot;http://wptavern.com/vienna-austria-to-host-wordcamp-europe-2016&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4764:&quot;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/wceu-2016-announcement.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/wceu-2016-announcement.png?resize=1022%2C511&quot; alt=&quot;photo credit: RubenSutiloFoto&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-45848&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;https://europe.wordcamp.org/2015/how-we-selected-vienna-the-wordcamp-europe-2016-host-city/&quot;&gt;RubenSutiloFoto&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The local WordPress community in Seville welcomed a diverse group of attendees to &lt;a href=&quot;https://europe.wordcamp.org/2015/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordCamp Europe 2015&lt;/a&gt; over the weekend. WordPress enthusiasts and professionals from Europe and beyond made strategic connections, &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/no_fear_inc/status/615149090825965568&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;contributed&lt;/a&gt;, found &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/WCEurope/status/615286319305084929&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;jobs and employees&lt;/a&gt;, and enjoyed presentations from a selection of world class speakers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot; width=&quot;550&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;Seville has got the imaginative juices flowing and led to some exciting changes of life direction &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/wceu?src=hash&quot;&gt;#wceu&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Fiona Barnes (@Barnes_Fiona) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/Barnes_Fiona/status/615137692293197824&quot;&gt;June 28, 2015&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot; width=&quot;550&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;Very happy to announce &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/SergeyBiryukov&quot;&gt;@SergeyBiryukov&lt;/a&gt; will be joining &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/yoast&quot;&gt;@yoast&lt;/a&gt;, spending 50% of his time on WP core. &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/WCEU?src=hash&quot;&gt;#WCEU&lt;/a&gt; was productive.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Joost de Valk (@jdevalk) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/jdevalk/status/615219329035042816&quot;&gt;June 28, 2015&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At the conclusion of the WordCamp, organizers &lt;a href=&quot;https://europe.wordcamp.org/2015/how-we-selected-vienna-the-wordcamp-europe-2016-host-city/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;announced&lt;/a&gt; that the 2016 event will be held in Vienna, Austria, June 24 &amp;#8211; 26. Applications for the host city were &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordcamp-europe-now-taking-applications-for-2016-host-city&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;opened&lt;/a&gt; in March and &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/applications-to-host-wordcamp-europe-2016-closing-soon&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;closed&lt;/a&gt; at the end of April.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The WordCamp Europe organization team received strong applications from the WordPress communities in Vienna, Bratislava, and Berlin. Some of the most important criteria in the selection process included organizer experience, location, venue, contributor day, and budget.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Berlin was ruled out due to lack of experience among the organizers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;The reason that we ruled out Berlin is that there hasn’t yet been a WordCamp in Berlin and we felt that the team needed more WordCamp organizing experience,&amp;#8221; Siobhan McKeown said in the official &lt;a href=&quot;https://europe.wordcamp.org/2015/how-we-selected-vienna-the-wordcamp-europe-2016-host-city/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;announcement&lt;/a&gt;. &amp;#8220;We’d love to see a WordCamp Berlin in the future – such a wonderful city needs a wonderful WordCamp.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Although Berlin has actually hosted three WordCamps in the past, including &lt;a href=&quot;https://central.wordcamp.org/wordcamps/germany-2010/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordCamp Germany 2010&lt;/a&gt;, WordCamps Berlin &lt;a href=&quot;http://wpde.org/wordcamp/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;2012&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://wpcamp.de/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;2013&lt;/a&gt;, other more weighty factors pushed Bratislava and Vienna ahead as potential host cities.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Bratislava brought a strong and diverse local team to the table, but Vienna ultimately surpassed the other applicants when it came down to logistics.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;In the end, the venue, location, and available dates for the WordCamp won out,&amp;#8221; McKeown said. &amp;#8220;We loved the Bratislava application, but none of the venues were completely suitable for our event.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;The venue in Vienna, however, was perfect. We also have 100% confidence in the Vienna local team: they organized a successful WordCamp Vienna in 2015, and Paolo Belcastro, the lead applicant for WordCamp Europe 2016, has been involved in WordCamp Europe for the past three years. This means that the local team will have a leader with a ton of WCEU experience.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;With a successful &lt;a href=&quot;https://europe.wordcamp.org/2015/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordCamp Europe 2015&lt;/a&gt; in the bag, the organization team will now set its sights on Vienna and continue its year round planning efforts. Speaker selection usually begins five or six months in advance for this event, so those planning to apply have plenty of time to prepare.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 29 Jun 2015 17:54:04 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}}}}}}}}}}}}s:4:&quot;type&quot;;i:128;s:7:&quot;headers&quot;;a:10:{s:6:&quot;server&quot;;s:5:&quot;nginx&quot;;s:4:&quot;date&quot;;s:29:&quot;Mon, 13 Jul 2015 19:20:23 GMT&quot;;s:12:&quot;content-type&quot;;s:8:&quot;text/xml&quot;;s:14:&quot;content-length&quot;;s:6:&quot;180623&quot;;s:10:&quot;connection&quot;;s:5:&quot;close&quot;;s:4:&quot;vary&quot;;s:15:&quot;Accept-Encoding&quot;;s:13:&quot;last-modified&quot;;s:29:&quot;Mon, 13 Jul 2015 19:15:16 GMT&quot;;s:15:&quot;x-frame-options&quot;;s:10:&quot;SAMEORIGIN&quot;;s:4:&quot;x-nc&quot;;s:11:&quot;HIT lax 249&quot;;s:13:&quot;accept-ranges&quot;;s:5:&quot;bytes&quot;;}s:5:&quot;build&quot;;s:14:&quot;20130911040210&quot;;}|no

|4|1|2015-07-08 19:19:48|2015-07-08 19:19:48|This is an example page. It's different from a blog post because it will stay in one place and will show up in your site navigation (in most themes). Most people start with an About page that introduces them to potential site visitors. It might say something like this:

&lt;blockquote&gt;Hi there! I'm a bike messenger by day, aspiring actor by night, and this is my blog. I live in Los Angeles, have a great dog named Jack, and I like pi&amp;#241;a coladas. (And gettin' caught in the rain.)&lt;/blockquote&gt;

...or something like this:

&lt;blockquote&gt;The XYZ Doohickey Company was founded in 1971, and has been providing quality doohickeys to the public ever since. Located in Gotham City, XYZ employs over 2,000 people and does all kinds of awesome things for the Gotham community.&lt;/blockquote&gt;

As a new WordPress user, you should go to &lt;a href=&quot;http://novo-construction/wp-admin/&quot;&gt;your dashboard&lt;/a&gt; to delete this page and create new pages for your content.
